Lu Bohong Reports on Flood Relief Work in Shandong

The Shanghai Fundraising Association for Flood Relief in Various Provinces on Yunnan Road publicly appointed Lu Bohong and others to go to Shandong to investigate and provide urgent relief. Mr. Lu and others promptly made arrangements to go to Shandong, and planned and carried out the work with diligence and care. The Association has reported to various newspapers that it has recently received two letters from Mr. Lu and others, reporting on the progress of flood relief work in Shandong. The following is a transcription of the letters:

First Letter

The letter dated October 1st states, "Respectfully, we received your association's telegram remitting 130,000 yuan for flood relief in Shandong, and have telegraphed confirmation of receipt. We immediately consulted with the local relief agencies to determine the distribution method based on the severity of the disaster. The details are presented below: (1) The 25 shelters in Jinan, housing approximately 16,000 disaster victims, were allocated 40,000 yuan for relief. (2) The shelters in the 10 disaster-stricken counties, housing approximately 270,000 disaster victims, were allocated 60,000 yuan for subsidies. (3) The Jinan Disaster Victims' Hospital No. 1 and No. 2 were established in Jinan. Hospital No. 1 has monthly expenses of 1,400 yuan, totaling 8,400 yuan for six months, plus 1,000 yuan for start-up costs, totaling 9,400 yuan. Hospital No. 2 has monthly subsidies of 500 yuan, totaling 3,000 yuan for six months, plus 600 yuan for start-up costs, totaling 3,600 yuan. (4) Disaster Victims' Hospitals were established in Jining, Caozhou, and Juye, each with monthly expenses of 800 yuan, totaling 2,400 yuan for the three locations. For six months, the total expenses are 14,400 yuan, plus 900 yuan per location for start-up costs, totaling 2,700 yuan for the three locations, for a total of 17,100 yuan. The above five hospitals require a total of 30,100 yuan. Regarding the distribution of relief funds, (1) the 40,000 yuan for the Jinan shelters has been allocated to the Jinan Municipal Government for distribution as agreed, and representatives from our association will visit the shelters from time to time to inspect and prevent abuses. (2) Due to the inconvenience of transportation and the complexity of the situation in the 10 disaster-stricken counties, the 60,000 yuan for the shelters will be entrusted to the Shandong Provincial Relief Association for responsible distribution based on the severity of the disaster, and representatives from our association will be dispatched to conduct on-site investigations, with reports to follow in due course. (3) Hospital No. 1 in Jinan was originally a newly established orphanage for disaster-affected children with inadequate facilities and successive deaths. Our association has dispatched personnel to be responsible for management and has requested five nuns from the local Catholic Church Hospital to provide voluntary services, including diagnosis and nursing, which will gradually improve the situation. However, the hospital can only accommodate 170-180 patients, and there is a shortage of rooms due to the increasing number of patients. Hospital No. 2 was originally a hospital established by the local Catholic Church in Dongguan. Our association has increased the number of beds by 100, and the nuns from the hospital also provide voluntary services. The hospital is now full. (4) The hospitals in Jining, Caozhou, and Juye are also being prepared by Mr. Wan Binlai, a Catholic priest who has been handling disaster relief for many years with outstanding results and is admired by the local community. Details will be reported in due course."

Second Letter

The letter dated October 13th states, "We received your kind letter of October 7th yesterday, and we are pleased to hear that the previous letter has reached you. The work of the Jinan office can be divided into two categories: (1) Entrusted by the Jinan Municipal Government, the 24 disaster victim shelters in Jinan City were handed over to our association for organizing mobile medical treatment. We personally witnessed that the disaster victims were both afflicted by disaster and disease, and their situation was extremely pitiful. The hospitals in Jinan City, including the two established by our association, are still insufficient. In order to avoid neglecting the sick and injured, it is necessary to organize mobile medical treatment. However, this matter is significant and the funds are limited. After repeated discussions, we invited twelve nuns from the medical departments of various monasteries in the local Catholic Church to form three groups and visit each shelter in turn every day for mobile medical treatment. If any patients have slightly more serious conditions, they are sent to the hospital for diagnosis and treatment. Since the implementation, the results have been good. The nuns who are invited to serve are not only volunteers, but also have the principle of faith and the spirit of loving others, so they serve with enthusiasm and are loved by the sick. (2) Entrusted by the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Relief Association, our association distributed 50,000 yuan of its urgent relief funds on its behalf. 25,000 yuan has now arrived in Jinan. Because it is urgent relief and the disaster victims are in dire need of relief, without delay, we used our association's flags and armbands and dispatched four of our association's investigators and two relief workers from the Shandong Provincial Relief Association on October 9th, together with two relief workers from the Jining branch of the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association, for a total of eight people. On October 11th, they set off from Jining in three groups to various areas that were most severely affected by the disaster for on-site investigation and distribution. The principles of relief are: 1. To go to the disaster areas with the most severe disasters; 2. To relieve the most distressed disaster victims. The distribution of relief funds is as follows: (1) 10,000 yuan for Juancheng (the county where Dongzhuang, the breach in the Yellow River, is located. This Yellow River disaster hit the area first, so the disaster is extremely severe); (2) 10,000 yuan for Dongping (After the northeastern flow of the Yellow River breach entered the area, it was connected to Mount Tai, and mountain floods broke out, and all the mountain water flowed into the county, attacking from both sides, and the disaster was extremely severe); (3) 5,000 yuan for Shouzhang (Dongdu in this county was flooded by the Yellow River, and the water from Mount Tai also flowed in from Shandong Ping, but the area is relatively small). The above distribution of relief funds was carefully discussed by us twice in Jining with the local branch, local officials, and impartial gentry, based on the severity and urgency of the disaster, the amount of relief funds distributed, and the order of relief. The discussions were considered fair, and the departing personnel can also uphold your dedication to disaster relief and embrace the spirit of being practical and truly helping the disaster victims. Therefore, it is expected that the future will be properly handled, and future situations will be reported at any time."

It can be seen that Mr. Lu and others have planned carefully and worked hard, and the Flood Relief Association is employing capable people and conducting investigations diligently, which is especially praised by people in the community.

Shanghai's Anti-Smoking Campaign is in Full Swing; Self-Surrender for Smokers to End in Four Days; Smoking Offenders to be Detained, Fined, and Subjected to Compulsory Rehabilitation; Informants to be Rewarded

The Municipal Public Security Bureau understands the total number of smokers and the amount of smoking in this city in order to establish a standard for gradual annual reduction. Therefore, it is conducting smoker registration. However, the voluntary registration has been ongoing since July and has lasted for four months. After four days, it will be the period of compulsory registration, and self-surrender for smokers will be stopped. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency investigated and recorded the details as follows:

Last Four Days of Registration Opportunity

The voluntary registration period was originally from July to September of this year. However, the Public Security Bureau extended it for one month until the end of this month because a part of the smokers in this city had not understood the registration procedures by the end of September. There are only four days left now, from today (28th) to the 31st. These four days are the last opportunity for smokers in this city to register voluntarily. The Public Security Bureau's third general survey of smokers will also end on the 31st. The total number of smokers found in the survey in this city is almost the same as the total number of smokers currently registered. However, there are still a few who have not gone to the Public Security Bureau to register. If they register in these four days, they will not violate the ban and will not be subject to arrest.

Stopping Self-Surrender and Rewarding Informants

Once these four days have passed, on November 1st of next month, the arrest of smokers will begin, and self-surrender will be stopped. Those found to be smoking privately will be fined from 50 yuan to 300 yuan according to regulations and then forced to register. During the period of compulsory registration from November to December, the Public Security Bureau will reward citizens of this city who report smokers. A method is currently being drafted, and it will be implemented after approval by the bureau chief in order to thoroughly eliminate smokers and achieve the purpose of strict anti-smoking in this city.

Registration Deadline, Fines, and Compulsory Rehabilitation

The smoker registration period of the Public Security Bureau is currently set to end at the end of this year. After that, smokers who are found to be smoking privately by the Public Security Bureau will be considered smoking offenders, and they will be fined and then sent to a rehabilitation hospital for compulsory rehabilitation.

Severe Military Punishment for Private Transportation and Establishment

In this strict anti-smoking campaign in this city, the Public Security Bureau has also decided on punishment methods for cases of privately transporting tobacco and establishing smoking dens for people to smoke. Those found to be privately transporting or selling tobacco will be sent to military law agencies for military punishment, and all their property will be confiscated according to regulations.

Smoking Cessation Methods During the Voluntary Period

There must be many citizens in this city who want to apply for smoking cessation to the Public Security Bureau during this remaining four-day voluntary registration period. The smoking cessation application methods stipulated by the Public Security Bureau are specially supplemented below for the reference of citizens in this city. The original text of the smoking cessation application is as follows: "Smokers who request smoking cessation during the voluntary registration period must fill out an application form and a guarantee letter, which can be obtained from the sub-bureaus of the Public Security Bureau. After investigation by the Public Security Bureau, they will be exempted from being sent to a smoking cessation hospital for compulsory rehabilitation. When discharged from the hospital, they must fill out a written guarantee that they will not smoke again and file it for future reference."

City Police Interrogate Suspected Smokers on the Streets; Arresting Those Who Sell and Eat at Night; Interrogating Those with Smoking Faces

The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau is handling smoker registration. The voluntary registration deadline is the 31st of this month, and compulsory registration will be required from next month. The Municipal Public Security Bureau's sub-bureaus in Nanshi and the city specially dispatched a large number of police officers to Xiaobeimen, Laobeimen, Ximen Nanshi and other places in the past two days. In the past two days, a total of one hundred and fifty to sixty smokers who secretly sold and ate at night were arrested. If anyone walking on the road has a smoking face, the police will also interrogate whether they are smoking opium and urge them to register quickly to avoid being forcibly detained and punished.

Page 11

Special Zone Telephone Charges Based on Usage: Municipal Federation Expresses Disagreement; Hopes the Municipal Council Considers Public Opinion and Changes the Policy to Avoid Major Disputes

Regarding the issue of increased telephone charges in the Shanghai Special Zone, after the Municipal Council hired telephone experts from China, Britain, the United States, and Japan to form a special committee to conduct research, it has been completed and a report has been submitted to the Municipal Council for review. The charging method stipulates that stores pay 10 yuan per month for 150 calls, and residences pay 6.5 yuan per month for 100 calls. Exceeding this number, each call will be charged 3 cents. The emphasis on charging based on usage has aroused attention from all parties.

A reporter from Dagong News Agency met with the person in charge of the Special Zone Citizens' Federation yesterday, who stated that the outline of the telephone special committee's report is purely based on the interests of the telephone company, which is deeply regrettable. The charging method proposed by the committee has been repeatedly opposed by the Federation in letters, but it has not been adopted, and the principle of charging based on usage is still maintained, which disappoints all users in the concession. At a time when Shanghai's social economy is collapsing and commerce is declining, the special committee has still failed to take these key points into consideration and insists on maintaining the company's profit at all costs, imposing restrictions on the calls needed for business, which severely affects commercial development. As for the suffering felt by users in the concession, the issue of paying fees for Chinese-rented calls has not been resolved by the special committee. Chinese-rented calls have long been equipped with automatic switchboards, and both parties should use direct dialing methods. However, the Shanghai Telephone Company, due to the fee issue, has inserted manual switchboards, causing users to waste both time and money. Now that the emphasis is on charging based on usage, the fees for these calls should be abolished to be reasonable, but the committee has failed to do so, which is unfair.

The Federation, as a citizens' group, does not agree with this method. Fortunately, the final decision-making power rests with the Municipal Council, and it is hoped that the Council can consider the public opinion of taxpayers and change the policy to avoid major disputes. Otherwise, the Federation will convene users to jointly discuss countermeasures to achieve the goal of canceling the price increase.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Releases the Full Text of the Bankruptcy Law and its Implementation Regulations; Both Creditors and Debtors Should Pay Attention

Since the Bankruptcy Law was promulgated on July 17th of this year and implemented on October 1st, debtors who cannot repay their debts may, according to the provisions of the law, request reconciliation from the court or the Chamber of Commerce. Currently, the Hua Ying Pharmacy, Minghua Bank, Shanghai Guohuo Company, Que Le Pharmacy, and other four companies have requested the Chamber of Commerce to reconcile debts in accordance with the law. However, the Bankruptcy Law stipulates that a request for reconciliation must be accompanied by a statement of financial status, a list of creditors and debtors, a proposed plan for reconciliation with creditors, and a guarantee for the implementation of the proposed liquidation method. The applicants often fail to provide the above documents, which delays the process after being ordered by the Chamber of Commerce to supplement them. At the same time, creditors also have questions about the legal procedures for the Chamber of Commerce to handle reconciliation and convene meetings. In order to clarify matters for both creditors and debtors, the Chamber of Commerce has published the full text of the Bankruptcy Law, consisting of four chapters and 159 articles, and the full text of the Implementation Regulations, consisting of six articles, in the 10th issue of Volume 15 of the Commercial Monthly. This issue is now published and can be used as a reference for debtors and creditors.

Zhejiang General Association Held its 11th General Membership Meeting Yesterday; More Than 200 Attended and Passed More Than a Dozen Important Motions; Also Sent a Telegram to Chairman Jiang Supporting the Special Anti-Smoking Law

According to the Riri News Agency, the Zhejiang General Association held its 11th General Membership Meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday on the fourth floor of the Ningbo Native Association on Xizang Road. More than 200 members attended, and Chu Huiseng, Wang Xiaolai, Yin Zhufu, and others were elected as the presidium. More than a dozen important motions were passed, and a telegram was sent to Chairman Jiang supporting the special anti-smoking and anti-drug crime law. Details are as follows:

Chairman's Report

After the formalities were completed, Chairman Yin Zhufu first reported on the association's work over the past year, which can be divided into four points: (1) Initiated the organization of the Jiaxu Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association, with the association responsible for relief in 13 counties and implementing work relief during the spring relief; (2) Advocated for the construction of inland water conservancy projects, some of which have been implemented; (3) Advocated for the reduction of surcharges; (4) Strove to increase jurisdiction over the Shengsi Islands, to be handled jointly by the two provincial governments. Then, Chairman Chu reported on the relief strategy for 1934.

Discussion of Proposals

(1) Supporting Chairman Jiang's special anti-smoking and anti-drug crime law, proposed by the board of directors, decided by the general meeting to send a telegram to Chairman Jiang (the original telegram will follow). (2) Proposal to revitalize sericulture, proposed by the board of directors, passed after deliberation. (3) Proposal to suggest that the Ministry of Industry establish a National Fisheries University and restore the Zhejiang Dinghai Fisheries School, proposed by the board of directors, resolved to change it to a fisheries college and establish branches in coastal provinces. (4) Proposal to promote the improvement of domestic tobacco leaves, with the association preparing funds to purchase American seeds and distribute them to various tobacco-producing areas in the province for trial planting, passed after deliberation. (5) Proposal to suggest that the Zhejiang Provincial Government construct water conservancy projects in western Zhejiang, especially to first dredge the north and south lakes of Yuhang to maintain the livelihoods of the people in Hangzhou, Jiaxing, and Huzhou, passed after deliberation. (6) Discussion on the issue of salt production in the coastal areas of Zhejiang, resolved to combine it with the eighth proposal, which is to suggest that the government 制余姚场盐版 implement a system where manufacturers have their own 盐版 to relieve salt farmers and permanently eliminate salt tides, and hand it over to the board of directors for handling. (7) Proposal that the household donations of the security corps should not be incorporated into the house donations and should not be apportioned according to farmland, proposed by Cha Zhongjian, with Chairman Chu's report attached. Member Tong Yihan also sent a letter advocating that the personnel and firearms of the backbone team should be removed, leaving the defense empty, and requested a proposal to save the situation, resolved to hand over the proposals of the two members Cha and Tong to the new board of directors for handling.

Temporary Proposals

Zhang Weichun and Qian Youlan proposed (1) to suggest that the provincial government engage in dredging the Cao'e River, passed after deliberation, with the association convening experts from the counties along the river and water conservancy experts to jointly formulate specific measures and suggest that the government implement them within a time limit. (2) To clearly define the Spring Festival for farmers in Zhejiang Province, resolved to hand it over to the board of directors to propose appropriate measures to replace farmers' superstitious behaviors. (3) To exempt small boats used by farmers in the countryside from license donations, resolved to hand it over to the board of directors to reiterate the previous request. (4) To telegraph the Drug Enforcement Supervisor to order the immediate ban on poppies and change to planting rice, wheat, and other grains in Yunnan, Guizhou, Sichuan, Shaanxi, Gansu, and other provinces to enrich the people's food and military supplies, passed and handed over to the board of directors to draft the telegram. (5) To suggest that the Zhejiang Provincial Government's Department of Construction plan to improve tobacco leaves, passed and handed over to the board of directors for handling. (6) Director Yu Hualong proposed to amend the membership fees, resolved that those who pay 50 yuan or more at one time would be permanent members. (7) Xu Zuoliang proposed that the association's funds be used to purchase real estate, handed over to the board of directors. (8) To suggest that the provincial government issue an order to plant bamboo along the dikes to protect the dikes, handed over to the board of directors for detailed discussion.

Guangdong Hospital Yesterday's Football Charity Match: Hong Kong vs. Guangdong Ends in a 2-2 Draw

The Guangdong Hospital in Zhabei, Shanghai, invited the Hong Kong and Guangdong football teams participating in the National Games to Shanghai for a charity match at the City Center Stadium to raise funds. Zhang Fakui, the former commander of the Fourth Army, was invited to perform the opening kick-off ceremony. The match started at 3 PM, with Chang Liqiu as the referee. The two teams played quite politely, abandoning the overly aggressive attitude they displayed when competing for the championship during the National Games, which won the audience's praise. The Guangdong team was well-organized and attacked more than defended. The Hong Kong team's offense was relaxed, and the lineup changed greatly in the second half, showing some tension. They seized the opportunity to score two goals, achieving a commendable draw. The details of the match are as follows:

Zhang Fakui General Performs Opening Ceremony

With the sound of a silver whistle, General Zhang kicked the ball to the Guangdong center forward. The Hong Kong team intercepted it midway, and Li Shuoyou went straight in along the side, creating a strong impression, but it was only a fleeting moment. Guangdong launched a major attack, circling the enemy territory and shooting twice, but the aim was inaccurate. After that, it was one in and one out, attacking and defending alternately, the performance was relaxed. Since they were brothers, the two sides played very friendly, without any fierce fighting. Stray balls appeared in front of both teams' goals from time to time. The Guangdong team attacked more than defended. Tan Jiangbai, the right inside forward, received support from the right, dribbled across the goal, and before the inner defensive line could react, he swept the ball with his left foot. The ball went from the left corner of the goal into the net, only ten minutes into the game.

1-0

Hong Kong was one goal behind and immediately launched a counterattack. Zhuo Shijin opened up his kicking and He Jiaqi volunteered, taking long shots outside the enemy inner defensive line one after another, but none hit the target. At this time, Guangdong forward Tan Jiangbai appeared in the enemy陣, very active, and coordinated with Chen Zhenhe. The Hong Kong defense worked hard to resist and avoided disaster. Not long after, Guangdong winger Yang Shuiyi dribbled deeper again, passing to Tan Jiangbai, who shot the ball, but it was too high and was caught by the goalkeeper. Although the Hong Kong team took the opportunity to counterattack from time to time, the coordination of the forwards was poor and weak, so they could not penetrate deeply. Later, they gathered a large force again and attacked the Guangdong inner defensive line from left and right. Sure enough, Li Zhaorong saw an opportunity and charged forward, but the ball was blocked by the Guangdong goalkeeper, and he gained nothing. The first half ended 1-0.

Avoiding the Enemy Defense to Create a Tie

After lemon time, the Hong Kong team's lineup changed greatly. Center forward He Jiaqi was injured in the first half and was replaced by Cao Guicheng. After the change of sides, He was transferred to goalkeeper, Huang Hua took over as defender, and Yang Benhan took the right wing. After the kick-off, the attack was unsuccessful. Guangdong's Chen Zhenhe launched a solo attack, continuing his efforts, penetrating deep into the hinterland, and passing the ball to Tan Jiang, the situation was very dangerous. Tan kicked the ball and Liang Xianzhan caught it, otherwise it would have been over. Guangdong's momentum did not abate, and they crossed the enemy陣. Chen, Tan, Huang, Yang and other forwards shot several times one after another, and the enemy goal was as fragile as an egg. Fortunately, good luck prevailed and they avoided disaster. The situation changed, and the Hong Kong army penetrated deeply. Li Zhaorong got the ball and flicked it lightly, avoiding the enemy's defense and scoring a goal, creating a tie.

Ending in a 2-2 Draw

After that, both sides played enthusiastically, using surprising tactics, charging into the enemy territory, and the performance gradually became exciting. Hong Kong, having recovered lost ground, boosted its morale, and the forwards galloped into Guangdong's territory, attacking several times, but were all saved. Guangdong waited for an opportunity and made a comeback. After a brief melee, Yang Shuiyi sent the ball to the front of Hong Kong's goal. Zheng Jiliang missed his footing, and Tan Jiangbai kicked the ball, and it went into the net. Hong Kong was one goal behind again, unwilling to give in, they made a comeback, and the soldiers did their best. Midfielder Huang Meishun carried the ball out, dribbled past two passes, and kicked the ball, skimming past the front. Continuing their efforts, they continued to attack fiercely. Cao Guicheng sent the ball flying from the right towards the goal. He jumped up and pushed the ball with the momentum. The goalkeeper hurriedly blocked it, but the ball slipped to the goal post. Zhuo Shijin, who was waiting for the right moment, kicked it gently, and the whole game ended 2-2.

Education News: Statistics on Chinese Students Studying Abroad in the Last Six Years

The status of Chinese students studying abroad in the last six years has been compiled by the Ministry of Education. The main points are recorded below:

(1) In 1929, 24 public-funded students and 333 self-funded students studied in European countries. The total number of public and private students was 357, including 49 in the UK, 86 in Germany, 165 in France, and 56 in Belgium. One in Italy. In the Americas, there were 54 public-funded students and 218 self-funded students. The total number of public and private students was 272, all of whom were in the United States. In other countries, there were 11 public-funded students and 1,017 self-funded students. The total number of public and private students was 1,028, including 1,025 in Japan, 1,025 in Japan. Egypt, India, the Philippines and Annam have a total of three people. The above total of Europe, America and other regions is 1,657 people.

(2) In 1930, 23 public-funded students and 258 self-funded students studied in European countries. The total number of public and private students was 281, including 16 in the UK, 66 in Germany, and 142 in France. There were 42 people in Belgium, 2 in Italy, 10 in Austria, 2 in Denmark, and 1 in the Netherlands. In the Americas, there were 158 people in the United States, including 24 public-funded students and 134 self-funded students. In other countries, there were 590 people in Japan, including 34 public-funded students and 556 self-funded students. The above total of Europe, America and other regions is 1,029 people.

(3) In 1931, 24 public-funded students and 222 self-funded students studied in European countries. The total number of public and private students was 246, including 25 in the UK, 84 in Germany, 106 in France, and 26 in Belgium. One in Italy, three in Sweden, and one in Switzerland. In the Americas, there were 11 public-funded students and 108 self-funded students. The total number of public and private was 119, including 115 in the United States and 4 in Canada. In other countries, there were 4 public-funded students and 81 self-funded students. The total number of public and private students was 85, including 83 in Japan. One in India, one in the Philippines. The above total of Europe, America and other regions is 450 people.

(4) In 1932, 25 public-funded students and 216 self-funded students studied in European countries. The total number of public and private students was 241, including 56 in the UK, 64 in Germany, and 108 in France. There were 10 in Belgium, 3 in Austria, and 99 in the United States for public and private expenses in the Americas. There was one person in Canada. In other countries, there were 2 public-funded students and 233 self-funded students. The total number of public and private was 235, including 227 in Japan. Five in Egypt, one in India, and two in the Philippines. The above total of Europe, America and other regions is 576 people.

(5) In 1933, 44 public-funded students and 164 self-funded students studied in European countries. The total number of public and private students was 208, including 75 in the UK, 68 in Germany, and 45 in France. There were 14 people in Belgium, 2 in Italy, 1 in Switzerland, 2 in Austria, and 1 in Denmark. There were 49 public-funded students and 138 self-funded students in the Americas. The total number of public and private students was 187, with 186 in the United States and one in Canada. The above total of Europe, America and other regions is 621 people.

(6) In 1934, 82 public-funded students and 172 self-funded students studied in European countries. The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education Orders County Education Bureaus to Instruct All Schools to Focus on Practical Work

Should Reduce Meetings That Are Merely Formal

In order to ensure that everything is done and no time is wasted

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education recently pointed out that school leaders often focus on formalities and hold various meetings for school affairs. There are several meetings every week, and most of the attendees at each meeting are the same. As a result, the principal and all teachers and staff are busy with meetings, overwhelmed and neglecting their work. Therefore, the provincial department specially ordered the county education bureaus to instruct all schools that in the future, all principals and teachers and staff should devote themselves to focusing on practical work, and should try to reduce the number of meetings that are merely formal. Meetings stipulated in various laws and regulations promulgated before and after may also be held by each school at its own discretion, provided that the nature is the same, the attendees are roughly the same, and the original spirit is not impaired. The general goal is to ensure that everything is done and no time is wasted.

Talks About Investigating Primary and Secondary Education

Based on the Oral Proposal of Dr. Monroe

However, the Investigation Work Is Quite Complicated and Cannot Be Done Immediately

The China Cultural Education Foundation held its ninth board of directors meeting in Shanghai yesterday to discuss subsidizing the Ministry of Education's compulsory education funds of 300,000 yuan. The case of primary and secondary education was decided to be postponed at that time. According to Sun Hongfen, the acting director of the association, the case was an oral proposal made to the association by American educator Monroe Chuan. He meant that there are now many more primary and secondary schools established in China than before, and there should be specific statistics as a basis for improvement. He also said that if he wanted to start the investigation, he could introduce his country's specialized personnel to cooperate. At that time, the association also believed that the number of middle schools in China has now increased to 3,000, and there should be detailed information on the teaching materials and administration of each school. Therefore, it was also proposed for discussion at this regular meeting. However, because the investigation work is quite complicated, the number of primary and secondary schools in various places is large, and a large number of specialized personnel are required to be done immediately. Moreover, the Ministry of Education also has the work of investigating primary and secondary schools every year, and Dr. Monroe is not a formal proposal, so the association decided to postpone it.

Tooth Knowledge Q&A (7) by Lin Jianxian

(Question 36) What is enamel?

(Answer) It is a layer of white, semi-transparent inorganic material, mostly composed of lime and a type of collagen. It is as hard as porcelain, covering the outside of the tooth crown to protect the softer tissues inside. The surface of the enamel layer is found where chewing occurs.

(Question 37) Why can enamel protect teeth?

(Answer) (1) Because it is very hard and resistant to friction, teeth can withstand daily chewing without deteriorating quickly. (2) Because it has no sensation and does not conduct cold or heat, it can eliminate or reduce the stimulation of cold or heat to the dental pulp.

(Question 38) What is enamel most afraid of?

(Answer) It is most afraid of acid, because acid can dissolve it. This layer is extremely important in the cause of cavities, which will be discussed later. It is also afraid of knocking or too heavy pressure, because although it is hard and resistant to friction, it is very brittle. If it is subjected to impact or biting on too hard things, it is easy to break.

(Question 39) What is dentin?

(Answer) All the hard tissue of the tooth, except for a thin layer of enamel, is dentin. It can be regarded as the main body of the tooth, forming the shape of the tooth. Dentin is a slightly yellowish bone-like substance, not as hard as enamel, but elastic and not easily broken. It also has many fine nerve endings running through it, so it has some sensation.

(Question 40) What is the function of dentin?

(Answer) (1) It supports the enamel and makes it strong and durable. Without this elastic dentin lining the inside, how could this thin, fragile enamel withstand daily chewing without breaking? (2) It works with the enamel to form a strong wall to protect the central pulp.

(Question 41) Is the inside of a tooth hollow?

(Answer) Yes, it is hollow. In the crown portion, there is a cavity in the middle of the dentin called the pulp chamber. There is also a slender hollow tube that runs from the pulp chamber straight to the tip of the root, called the root canal. The pulp chamber and root canal contain the pulp, just as bone marrow is contained in the bone.

(Question 42) What is the dental pulp?

(Answer) It is a bundle of soft tissue containing nerves, blood vessels, and odontoblasts. If the pulp is extracted, it looks like a two- or three-tenths of an inch thick string of muscle. Its nerves and blood vessels are connected to the external nerves and blood vessels from the apical foramen of the root.

Disease Knowledge Q&A by Cheng Hanzhang

(71) Cirrhosis of the Liver

(Question) What is cirrhosis of the liver?

(Answer) It is a disease in which the liver cells shrink due to various chronic irritations or chronic infectious diseases, parasites, etc., resulting in sclerosis.

(Question) What are the causes of cirrhosis?

(Answer) Most are caused by excessive drinking; secondly, by the overuse of chili, mustard, and pepper; or chronic infectious diseases such as tuberculosis, syphilis, and malaria; or biliary tract diseases such as liver cysts, parasites, etc.: and also because of new metabolic diseases (diabetes, gout) and poisoning (lead, arsenic, phosphorus, etc.), all of which are causes of this disease.

(Question) What are the symptoms of liver disease?

(Answer) In the early stages, there are only occasional gastrointestinal symptoms, such as loss of appetite, fullness in the stomach, nausea, constipation, or diarrhea. After the portal vein system is invaded, the characteristic symptoms are ascites (bloating), splenomegaly, diarrhea, hematemesis, melena, hemorrhoids, etc.

(Question) What is the external appearance of the patient's abdomen?

(Answer) The abdomen is distended due to ascites, and the subcutaneous veins are dilated due to portal vein congestion, resembling the meandering of snakes. The lower extremities and scrotum become swollen.

(Question) What are the changes in the liver itself?

(Answer) The liver is enlarged at first; soon it shrinks (atrophy).

(Question) Is there a jaundice-like change in skin color?

(Answer) Jaundice rarely occurs in the skin; but it presents the dirty yellow color characteristic of liver disease.

(Question) Is there anything abnormal about urination?

(Answer) Urine output is reduced, contains bile pigments, shows a native reaction, and sometimes contains glucose.

(Question) How long does this disease last?

(Answer) The course is very slow: about two or three years. It is milder in the first year or year and a half, and then becomes more severe, leading to death from weakness.

(Question) How can I diagnose this cirrhosis of the liver?

(Answer) As long as you pay attention to whether the patient is a heavy drinker, the liver is shrinking, there are symptoms of portal vein congestion, gastrointestinal bleeding, and edema of the lower body, it is very easy.

(Question) What is the prognosis of cirrhosis?

(Answer) Most cannot avoid death.

(Question) How to treat it?

(Answer) It can be divided into three types: etiological treatment, restorative treatment, and symptomatic treatment.

(Question) What is etiological treatment?

(Answer) If the patient is addicted to alcohol, drinking should be prohibited; if the patient has syphilis, anti-syphilitic treatment should be given.

(Question) What is restorative treatment?

(Answer) In addition to abstaining from alcohol, spicy spices should also be avoided, meat should be restricted, and drinking plenty of milk and eating more fruit is most appropriate.

(Question) What is symptomatic treatment?

(Answer) Laxatives such as potassium tartrate, calomel, and Carlsbad salt should be taken internally, and then cardiotonics and diuretics should be used. If breathing difficulties are caused by ascites, paracentesis can be performed to release the accumulated fluid.

The Medicine of Pain Relief (38) by Li Xing

Coal Tar Analgesics

These drugs are also very useful analgesics. The most important in this class are: (1) Acetanilid and (2) Phenacetin (=Acetphenetidin). In addition to relieving pain, these drugs can also reduce fever. Small oral doses can relieve headaches and neuralgia. Some headache powders in the United States contain one of these two as a key ingredient. Note that these drugs should not be taken in excessive amounts or for too long because they are very toxic. These drugs are also not suitable for pain relief from external injuries. Another drug equivalent to coal tar analgesics is Ayramidon (also known as Amidopyrinle), which has the same properties.

Hypnotics and Pain Relief

Pain and insomnia are directly related; pain leads to insomnia, and insomnia causes the body to suffer more damage. People without pain need sleep, and those with pain need it even more. Sleep is the most important form of rest. With sufficient sleep, painful areas can get sufficient rest and repair. Rest is an essential element in pain relief and reducing swelling, and sleep is the best rest, so improving restful sleep is also one of the methods of pain relief.

The use of hypnotics should not be used casually - there must be a reason for using them. Using them appropriately is beneficial to the body, while using them inappropriately can be harmful to the body. Although hypnotics are not analgesics, they can complement analgesics. Analgesics can increase the effectiveness of hypnotics, and hypnotics can also increase the effectiveness of analgesics. When pain is severe, taking analgesics and hypnotics at the same time can achieve double the effectiveness. This principle is called synergism in medicine. For milder pain, simply using a hypnotic to allow the patient to sleep peacefully is equivalent to relieving pain. However, hypnotics should not be taken for long periods of time to avoid becoming a habit. Sometimes using heat therapy, such as hydrotherapy and diathermy, can relieve pain on the one hand and induce sleep on the other, which is much better than taking analgesics and hypnotics for a long time. Although hypnotics help with rest, excessive use can harm the body, especially by destroying red blood cells. This is why it is said that using them appropriately is beneficial, and using them inappropriately is harmful. The method of using hypnotics is like this, and the same is true for any method. This is a fundamental principle of therapeutics that should be paid attention to.

Physiologically, hypnotics work by suppressing sensation and perception, making one less sensitive to external stimuli. In this way, mild pain almost becomes painless, and the patient's sleep is slightly prolonged, so the painful days seem shorter. Hypnotics should not be used too much, as too much can easily cause coma in the patient. Hypnotics also have a suppressive effect on the heart and respiratory system. Those with unhealthy livers and kidneys should not take these drugs. There are many such drugs, but due to space limitations, not all can be explained. The names of the important ones are listed below. As for how to take them or when to take them, please consult a doctor for guidance: Barbital, Luminal, Chloral bydrate, Paraldehyde, Sodium Bromide, Potassium Bromide, Calcium Bromide, Amyta, Hyoscine, Sulphonal, Trional, etc.

Topical Analgesic Drugs

Carbolic acid is a poison and is the most notable of the caustic drugs. However, if a small amount of this drug is applied externally, it can relieve pain and itching. For example, if you have a toothache in the middle of the night, take a small amount of cotton wool dipped in a drop of this drug and plug it into the cavity, and it will relieve the pain miraculously.

Picric acid has the same disinfection power as carbolic acid, but its causticity is far less than that of carbolic acid. The greatest use of picric acid is for minor burns. Its function is to relieve local pain and precipitate toxins.

Magnesium sulfate, when prepared as a saturated solution, also has a local analgesic effect. The method of use is to soak medicine or gauze in this liquid first and then apply it to the swollen and painful area. Add medicine water when the gauze or cotton wool is slightly dry. The effect of wet application day and night for pain relief is also not small. This medicine is completely beneficial and harmless. It is most suitable for inflamed and red parts.

Belladonna ointment has a local numbing effect on nerves, so it can relieve local pain. Applying it to inflamed parts is also one of the proper ways.

Tincture of Aconite (Tr.Aconite) applied to the skin first causes a tingling sensation, which then turns into a numbness, so it is very effective for relieving neuralgia.

Elementary Discussion of Pulmonary Tuberculosis (72) by Hu Jiayan

Chapter 12: Treatment of Pulmonary Tuberculosis

Section 3: Rest and Nutrition

Why do patients with this disease need rich nutrition? We know that the approach to treating pulmonary tuberculosis is simply to increase the body's resistance so that the lesions are surrounded by connective tissue, and they will naturally heal. To increase the body's resistance, we must first fully supply the raw materials for the body's vitality, that is, nutritious food. Therefore, the more nutritious and abundant the food for patients with this disease, the better, and it is very important in any stage. This method was very well understood even in the old days by the general public. Therefore, almost everyone knows to pay attention to whether patients with this disease have a good appetite. As a result, it is somewhat over-relied upon, and it is almost universally regarded as the only treatment method for this disease. In fact, this is not entirely true. Although it is extremely necessary to ingest a large amount of food, on the other hand, the limits of the stomach and intestines' digestive power should be taken into account. If this limit is exceeded, not only will it not be digested, but the excess food will harm the function of the stomach and intestines, which is very detrimental to the future of this disease. In addition, as nutritious food increases, body weight will naturally increase as a result; but whether a simple increase in body weight is of great help to this disease is uncertain. Even excessive fat accumulation in the heart and excessive absorption of water by the urinary organs are very harmful. Judging from the nature of the lesions, thin people are mostly prone to proliferative sclerosis, while obese people are the opposite. We only need to know the prognosis to imagine that obesity may not necessarily be beneficial to patients with this disease!

Healthy people usually need about 3,000 calories of food per day. The three elements of protein, fat, and carbohydrates should all be mixed and ingested. Patients with this disease need more, which can be increased to more than 4,000 calories per day, but they should also be mixed and ingested, and not be biased towards any one aspect. Among them, foods rich in nutrients, such as milk, eggs, beef, other animal meats, various fresh vegetables, and fruits, etc., are indispensable. People who only eat vegetarian food are not very suitable for this disease, because animal proteins are particularly important for nutrition and are not good to be lacking. Whether or not it is rich in vitamins is also very important for the treatment of this disease. Cod liver oil is particularly rich in vitamins A and D, and patients should also take it daily. (However, it should not be excessive, as it may impair appetite.) Alcohol is on the list of prohibitions; but occasionally taking a small amount of wine or beer can increase appetite, and even help sleep at night. In addition, there are countless artificially manufactured tonics sold on the market. Commonly seen ones, such as "Sanatogen," "Horlick's Malted Milk," and "Somatose," etc., are very worthwhile for patients with poor appetite and indigestion, because the amount of food they take every day is always too small. But if the patient has a very good appetite, it is simple and straightforward to ingest a large amount of food, because the material losses, when compared, are too far apart!

Free Talk: Starting from "Incomprehensible" by Yu

With a golden cudgel in hand, anyone is the "Great Sage Equaling Heaven." Lose that golden cudgel, and anyone will inevitably remain a monkey. Monkeys' tricks are pretty much the same. Don't think your hat is one foot three inches long and can overwhelm people. Don't think your sleeves are ten thousand feet wide and can contain the universe. Admittedly, my writing and Mr. A's may not be the best in the world, but neither is it the case that no one else exists besides you. "Zhu Bajie playing with an eagle, each to his own liking." You like playing with mummies, you like playing with skeletons, you like invoking the dead, you like selling your name with the dead, you like profiting from the dead, you like treating rags as treasures, you like treating "dried dung sticks" as delicacies. This is your interest, your addiction, your way of making a living. Whether your motives are pure or your opinions are brilliant, it is not necessary for indifferent passersby to inquire. However, if you set a standard from your narrow perspective, take a ruler to measure other people's articles, declare that this article does not meet my A-type standard, that this article is incomprehensible, that this article does not meet my C-type conditions, that this publication is fundamentally unreadable, this conflicts with my A-type standard. "Unreadable, then what is there to read?" Unfortunately, there is no follow-up. In fact, no follow-up is needed. It is already clear that all publications are unreadable. Only that authoritative scholar wearing a one foot three inch long hat, under the standard of the "measuring stick of heaven," can select and compile the unique, humorous, leisurely magazine. "Wang Mazi's dog skin plaster, only this one shop, no branches." Readers, please don't mistake the sign.

Naturally, this old brand is easy to recognize. Its core is the Public Security Jingling School, its façade is the Quotations Style. Although the content of the articles has been influenced by foreign devils and is no longer as superficial as "the world, after being united for a long time, must divide; after being divided for a long time, must unite," the expression of the articles, because of the worship of the dead, is still that cliché of "the world, after being united for a long time, must divide; after being divided for a long time, must unite." Please forgive my presumption. What I consider a cliché is definitely what you will never admit. The Quotations Style is precisely what you consider to be the characteristic that turns decay into magic: it is a "simple and easy," "leisurely and free," "elegant and relaxed" literary style, it is the "true color of Chinese people speaking Chinese." It is natural for Chinese people to speak Chinese. I remember that Koizumi Yakumo once advised Japanese students: if a person wants to be a writer, he should first have complete knowledge of the living spoken language of his country. Because a complete understanding of the living spoken language, no matter whether it is spoken by high-class people or low-class people, whether it is ordinary or unusual, is very necessary. Only in this way is excellent literature possible. However, we know that the language of the Quotations Style is by no means a living language. Even if such language is spoken, it is probably not understandable by vulgar people like me. Moreover, although this kind of outdated, extremely sour, deathly atmosphere seems concise and elegant to sophisticated people, when vulgar people like me smell this smell, they have to vomit for three days. Therefore, I think that instead of robbing graves and breaking coffins, digging out the bones of the dead to beg for inspiration, it is better to go to the streets and alleys, listen to old women's trivial talks, shrewish women's scoldings, vendors' quarrels, and merchants' talk about market conditions. That is so lively, wonderful, and characteristic. However, this kind of spoken language of petty city dwellers is despised and not happily studied by our official linguists. Then we have to ask, where do Chinese people start speaking Chinese? Concise wording, leisurely tone, Quotations Style, mind, why bother with all this? It is better to honestly retreat to the old nest of classical Chinese and write classical Chinese straightforwardly. Wouldn't it be more concise, more leisurely, more elegant, more circuitous, and more ancient to write classical Chinese? Why bring out the Quotations Style, which is between the two, and the Ming people, whose bones have already withered, to add an extra burden and reduce a dependence. As for people like us who cannot read Chinese smoothly and cannot understand foreign languages, we can only resign ourselves to fate and write articles that break twenty-eight teeth to cheat a living. At the same time, if we can follow the regulations set by the masters, "Chinese people speak Chinese," we should try our best to speak Chinese. Just as if we have a long gown to wear, we wear a long gown. If there is no long gown at hand, we have to wear a clumsy Western suit and be scolded by Mr. Ah Q as a "fake foreign devil," which is not a big deal. But asking me to wear a red tasseled hat, a yellow mandarin jacket, and thick-soled boots on my feet, and swagger through the streets, I will never do it, even if it means death.

Chu Kuang and Confucius by Chen Zizhan

(1)

When King Zhao of Chu heard Zizhong's plea for help, he immediately ordered people to lead troops to rescue Confucius and welcome him to the south.

At this time, Confucius was on the border between the states of Chen and Cai, surrounded by ruffians sent by the ministers of the two states, because they were afraid that he would go to Chu, and if he gained power, he would make it difficult for the neighboring states of Chen and Cai. The disciples who accompanied him were all sick from hunger because they had run out of food. Confucius was still full of energy, lecturing and playing the qin for them, without resting. Confucius seemed to be deliberately pretending to be calm and optimistic, to encourage his disciples to endure the current hardships and reduce their complaints against him.

Fortunately, Zizhong sought reinforcements from Chu, and the teacher and disciples were able to break through the siege and come to Chu.

The disciples who followed Confucius south this time were all top students of the Confucius School. According to the classification of the Confucius School: those famous for their virtue were Yan Yuan, Min Ziqian, Ran Boniu, and Zhong Gong; those famous for their language were Zai Wo and Zizhong; those famous for their politics were Ran You and Ji Lu; those famous for their literature were Ziyou and Zixia. Talented people gathered, and their reputation shook the times.

When King Zhao of Chu heard that Confucius and his disciples had arrived, he wanted to summon him and grant him a territory of seven hundred miles. So he gathered his ministers to discuss the matter.

At this time, a high-ranking official in the Chu court was Lingyin Zixi. When he heard King Zhao's intention to grant Confucius land, he was shocked and immediately raised several troublesome questions for King Zhao to answer.

"Does your majesty have diplomatic talents like Zizhong?"

"No."

"Does your majesty have auxiliary minister talents like Yan Hui?"

"No."

"Does your majesty have general talents like Zilu?"

"No."

"Does your majesty have left and right officials like Zai Yu?"

"No."

"There is something else we need to know. At first, our ancestors of Chu were enfeoffed by Zhou, but they were only third or fourth-class vassal states, so-called viscounts or barons with fifty miles. Now, Confucius has learned the principles of the enlightened kings of the three dynasties who ruled the world, and also understands how the Duke of Zhou and the Duke of Shao helped the royal family. If your majesty grants him seven hundred miles, then how can our Chu guarantee that our descendants will keep this territory of thousands of miles?"

"Looking at King Wen of Zhou in Feng and King Wu of Zhou in Hao, at first they were only lords of a hundred miles, but in the end they became kings of the world. Now, Confucius has obtained such a large piece of land, and he has many virtuous disciples to help him, which may not be a blessing for Chu."

When King Zhao of Chu heard Lingyin Zixi's words, he became hesitant. The rest of the civil and military officials were silent, and the meeting ended without a result.

(2)

In the autumn of this year, King Zhao of Chu unfortunately died in Chenghu. Confucius had hoped that he would gain power in Chu this time, but in the end he gained nothing. A sad tear flowed from his eyes when he heard the news of King Zhao's death.

It was a clear and crisp autumn day. Confucius was alone, driving his carriage to the suburbs to vent his frustration.

Just as Confucius was leaving the city, right in front of his carriage, a famous eccentric of Chu, called Jieyu, swaggered over, deliberately raising his voice and singing a song:

"Phoenix, oh phoenix!

Why has your virtue declined?

(You are originally a bird of peace and auspiciousness, why were you born in this turbulent time?)

The past need not be mentioned,

The future can still be made in time.

Forget it, forget it!

Now all the dog officials are terrible!"

Before this old man finished singing, he had already brushed past Confucius' carriage without turning his head.

Confucius was surprised by the old man's eccentricity and felt touched by his song. He quickly got out of the carriage, wanting to ask the old man for advice, but the old man had already slipped away, and they didn't even exchange a word.

Confucius watched the old man swagger towards the city, stunned for a while, before dejectedly turning his carriage back home.

As soon as Confucius got out of the carriage and entered the door, the old man's eccentricity flashed in his eyes again, and the old man's song started again:

"Phoenix, oh phoenix!

How has your virtue declined?

The ideal afterlife cannot be waited for,

The glorious ancient times need not be mentioned.

When the world is in order,

A sage can be made.

When the world is in disorder,

A sage must also be born.

Born in this day and age,

Only seek to avoid unnecessary sacrifice.

Happiness is as light as a feather,

But no one knows to take it and enjoy it.

Disaster is as heavy as the earth,

But no one knows to seek ease.

Forget it, forget it!

What virtues are there to boast to people?

How dangerous, how dangerous!

Draw a circle and turn around in it.

The mimosa has thorns, mimosa!

Please don't hinder me from walking!

I'd rather walk crookedly,

Please don't hurt my feet!"

Confucius looked at the old man's receding back and listened to the sad song he sang. It was like pouring a bucket of cold water on his burning heart of respecting the king and restoring the ancient ways. He couldn't help but sigh with emotion: "Alas! The bird does not appear, there is no hope for peace in the world, my life is over like this!"

The Myna and the Hen (Part 1) by Lin Shi

Mrs. Liao, the owner of the store, never spent a penny recklessly. In her eyes, even a small copper coin was as precious as a silver dollar. Everyone in the neighborhood knew this. To say nothing else, just consider the time her only son stole a large copper coin to buy fried rice candy. When she found out, she gave him a severe beating, making his face red and swollen. Everyone who saw it said it was pitiful. Even the old widow who lived in the same house felt she was too cruel. It was common for children to steal a few copper coins out of greed, so why be so ruthless?

But there are always exceptions in the world. Mrs. Liao allowed her son to raise a myna, and it was bought for four hundred cash. Four hundred cash was a large sum in her eyes, but she didn't feel the pain for buying the myna.

Perhaps it was because the myna was too clever and likable. For example, when Mrs. Liao's son gave it rice balls to eat, it would come over hopping and chirping, eating from his hand without any fear, and was very affectionate. Not only was it like this with its young master, but it was also like this when Mrs. Liao sometimes fed it when she was free. Its simple "gaga" chirping sounded like a child who could laugh and jump, clamoring for milk. It really made her smile from ear to ear.

Once, some distant and respectable guests came to the Liao household, so Mrs. Liao made an exception and bought four taels of meat, which was almost more than two hundred cash. As she was cutting the meat into slices in the kitchen with her thin lips pursed, the little myna "gaga gaga" flew in front of her. The old widow also walked in with a gray face. The old widow saw her cutting meat and said, as if to Mrs. Liao and as if to herself:

"In this day and age, you still have money to buy meat to eat. What a blessing!" Her eyes stared at the slices of bright red meat, and it seemed that the delicious taste had reached the tip of her tongue, and she was almost drooling.

"Oh, who would be willing to buy meat to eat? But when distant guests come, you have to make it look a little bit presentable, and there's really nothing else to do." As she spoke, Mrs. Liao thought to herself that everyone said this guest's family had hidden many silver dollars as white as lard. Mr. Liao wanted to borrow one or two hundred yuan to turn around in the store. Mrs. Liao was a very worldly person and understood this, so she had to flatter them.

Just at this moment, by accident, the myna snatched a small piece of meat and ran away. Mrs. Liao was so tired that she hobbled over on her unbound feet to grab it, and the old widow also helped generously and bravely. But the myna flew to the roof of the toilet and would not come down again, which made her curse "Damn it!" but it was still useless.

"Damn it! Bitch! People haven't eaten yet, and you want to eat it."

"Forget it," the old widow said, "just let it eat a piece. Mynas have to eat meat to be able to talk. A talking myna is worth money."

Outside the Wall by Shen Shengshi

After the weather turned cool, all kinds of small business boats on the riverbank stopped and came to do business, so the riverbank was much more lively than usual. The ragged children of the boat families, with messy hair and bare feet, were all chasing each other on the riverbank. Their various toys were all picked up from the garbage heap! Broken iron cans, broken bottles, a neatly trimmed white grain stalk, a slightly smooth pebble, or a small bamboo pole. The children often gathered in groups, fighting and arguing on the riverbank, cursing with vulgar and obscene tunes. It was as if these children had never been cared for by anyone in the world. They all grew up naturally, never had the opportunity to be loved by their parents, and never had the opportunity to go to school. They all grew up in a vague natural environment, almost the same situation as some stray dogs on the street.

Our school was on the riverbank, and the school gate faced the river directly. After class, I often walked to the riverbank with my colleagues to stroll around, so I often had the opportunity to see those wild children fighting and playing. They wore ragged clothes and rolled around on the ground without any worries. Their faces were covered with streaks of dirt, and thick yellow snot hung from the black nostrils to their lips, chasing each other and playing on the riverbank.

I always thought that no one in the world cared about those children.

The school was surrounded by a short wall. Often, those children would try to climb up the wall to peek, and when they saw the classrooms and various toys inside, it was as if they felt that inside the wall was a very novel world. They would climb on the wall and stare in fascination for a long time.

It often caused me a little uncomfortable feeling. It was only a wall, but why couldn't they climb in?

Once, I was returning to school from the street and saw from afar that there were four or five children climbing the wall again, but they couldn't climb up. So one of them came up with an idea. First, one squatted on the ground, and another child stood on his shoulders and sent him up to climb. After looking for a while, they switched to another one to look.

"A Jin, you come and look!"

"It's fun, it's a foreign school!"

"A Gen, you come and look too."

Perhaps everyone wanted to be the first to climb up, but the one acting as the foothold was not very willing, so they started quarreling.

This quarrel was very fierce. In the evening, they were still throwing stones on the riverbank. Bricks and stones flew from outside the wall into the school, like stray bullets, and two large panes of glass on the windows of two classrooms in the school were broken.

The next day, the principal came to the school and told a school worker to stand guard at the gate when there was nothing to do, and not to allow those wild children to play near the wall.

Jade Garment (1) by Xin Zhuojia

"Jade Garment, come——"

Whenever I called, this unfortunate child would immediately stand in front of me, fixing me with her round, apprehensive eyes, and putting on an unnatural, careful smile.

I always felt an unusual pain and uneasiness in my heart. When I saw her—when I saw her tattered clothes, her withered yellow hair, her round eyes, and her pale, bloodless face—this uneasiness and pain would surround me more heavily, oppressing me!

I could not pull this painful, arrow-like root sprout from my heart no matter what.

"Yes," I thought, "I should find a way to send her away! Send her to a women and children's relief center, a charity asylum, or some other place that takes in orphans. I can't let her suffer like this with me!"

I had such plans when the child was still far away in my hometown. My woman wrote to me, saying, "This is indeed a clever and bright child. I must bring her when I come. About her background—in fact, you should know…," my woman added. And without fear of trouble, she told me in more detail: "She is the daughter of my sixth blind cousin, and she is also the youngest. You should also know about their family situation… When her father was not yet blind ten years ago, he was already unable to support a family of eight. And her birth happened to coincide with the emergency of her father's blindness. Of course, the hat of all suffering and evil should be placed on her head. What else is there to argue about, such a fate—blinding her father's eyes as soon as she was born!…"

"When she was an infant—I saw it with my own eyes—they treated her like pigs and dogs, letting her lie alone in a straw nest, left to fend for herself. They gave her a little rice water or something like that to drink, but she grew up like a wild tree. Later, because of her intelligence and cleverness, she finally aroused the love of her mother and other passing uncles!

"Her father's eyes are the fatal wound of her whole family; for eight or nine years, they have relied solely on her mother's spinning and weaving hemp to make a living. The year before last, during the great flood, they sold her first older sister; last year, during the drought—the second; this year, it's her turn again.

"She comes running to me every day. When she sees me, she is more affectionate than her own mother. I really don't know why I especially like this child. Her hair, eyes, lips, even every word she says makes me feel pity and love.

"She often cries to me, saying:

""Aunt, they want to sell me! Sell me!… My mother—she wants to sell me to Feiyuan…"" I said, ""Child, no!"" But my words are of no use. They finally found a buyer from out of town and started negotiations about her price."

Differential Diagnosis of Gonorrhea in this City's Supplement of Shen Bao (Dr. Luo Minxiu)

Those with inflammatory diseases of the urethra and bladder invariably experience frequent urination, painful or difficult urination, and purulent discharge from the urethra, etc. Those who are unaware always regard these phenomena as characteristics of gonorrhea. However, it is not known that this condition is caused by inflammation of the mucous membrane inside the urogenital organs, which leads to functional disorders and the flow of purulent secretions due to redness, swelling, heat, and pain. It is essential to investigate the cause of the disease before discussing treatment. If another disease is treated with reckless gonorrhea treatment, or if it is indeed a gonorrhea disease and is mistaken for another disease, it is rare for the treatment to be effective. Therefore, differential diagnosis is an indispensable key point in clinical practice, and the method is not only visual examination, but also dyeing specimens and microscopic observation to explore the correct pathogen and seek practical treatment. If it is a gonorrhea-related disease, there should be evidence of gonococcus, and then treatment will be free of any concerns. The patient's spirit, economy, and time will benefit greatly.

Sun Weicai and Sons Hospital on Ningbo Road in the French Concession of Shanghai has been treating venereal diseases for more than 20 years. Based on their rich experience and their heart to help the world, they have specially prepared high-magnification microscopes for free examination. They have hired many male and female doctors to be responsible for

Britain and France Prepare to Implement Economic Sanctions Against Italy; Japan Awaits League of Nations Adjustment Committee Decision; Proposed Compromise Not Acceptable to Britain and Abyssinia

(Geneva) Britain and France today notified the League of Nations that they intend to boycott Italian exports and prohibit the transportation of raw materials to Italy. Britain is prepared to implement the ban immediately on the date determined by the League of Nations Adjustment Committee. France stated that it must implement the ban four days after the date determined by the committee to take the necessary steps. The committee is scheduled to meet on October 31. (Reuter, 26th)

(London) The proposal put forward by Italy, which could serve as the basis for resolving the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, has been forwarded to London by France. It is generally believed that the British government cannot accept this proposal, at least in the form known to the outside world. The government is currently maintaining close contact with the French authorities to jointly consider the various possibilities of initiating negotiations after the Italian proposal has been revised. Political figures also stated that the government has taken the necessary measures to implement sanctions against Italy, and the execution of these sanctions will not be interrupted until the Italo-Abyssinian dispute is definitively resolved. (Havas, 26th)

(London) Officials claim that Britain has received several proposals from Italy for resolving the Italo-Abyssinian war. However, it is generally believed that neither the British nor the French government can accept them. It is understood that this proposal is Mussolini's perceived fair method for handling the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. Its content is based on the talks between French Prime Minister Laval and the Italian ambassador in Paris, which were later conveyed to London by Laval. Reliable sources believe that the sanctions plan against Italy, which was decided by the British Privy Council on Thursday, will still be implemented and will not be affected by this proposal. (National Telegram, 26th)

Addis Ababa According to a report from our special correspondent, O'Chana, Abyssinian government officials stated that the government has not received any proposals from Italy regarding a solution to the Italo-Abyssinian dispute and only learned about the general outline from newspapers. Even if this proposal is formally submitted, it will not be acceptable to the Abyssinian government. (Havas, 26th)

British Financial Sanctions to be Implemented Starting Tomorrow

(London) The British government issued a public notice today explaining the financial sanctions against Italy that will be implemented on October 29. Any government within any Italian territory, any resident within Italian territory regardless of nationality, and any organization organized under Italian law in any location must be treated according to the Italo-Sanctions Regulations. Italians residing outside Italian territory are exempt. However, branches of Italian organizations outside Italy are also subject to sanctions. Branches of organizations organized in other countries but located within Italy are exempt. Banking activities that do not involve lending facilities, such as currency remittances and securities interest payments, are not prohibited. Unfulfilled portions of contracts are also subject to the prohibition. Violators of the British financial sanctions ban will be subject to imprisonment of up to two years or fines, or both. Organizations can also be punished if it is proven that the director, manager, or secretary knowingly or negligently violated the ban. (Reuter, 27th)

Italy Determined to Resist Sanctions; Must Distinguish Between Friend and Foe

(Rome) Mussolini stated in a speech here today that Italy will strive to struggle against the League of Nations' implementation of sanctions, so as to distinguish between friends and foes. He also stated that countries that treat Italy so unfairly must know that Italy is capable of self-sufficiency, just as Italian soldiers are capable of avenging the previous shame of Adowa. (National Telegram, 26th)

(Rome) This year marks the thirteenth anniversary of the Fascist Party's march on Rome. The entire nation has been mobilized and is prepared to cope with any eventuality. Those who wish to inflict the most shameful injustice on Italy must know that the Italian people are brave and unyielding and will not hesitate to sacrifice themselves to follow in the footsteps of the soldiers of the Battle of Adowa. These soldiers have already injected civilization into a corner of Africa. Italy is currently under the threat of economic sanctions. This kind of evil and absurdity is extreme and will only increase international disputes and poverty, and will be condemned by history. Italians, except for those who are outwardly concerned, will strive to defend themselves and will also know how to distinguish between friendly nations and enemies." (Havas, 26th)

(Rome) Tomorrow is the anniversary of the Fascist Party's march on Rome. The celebratory ceremony prepared by the government is nothing less than an expression of resistance to sanctions. Prime Minister Mussolini has already drafted a declaration to be read publicly in the Piazza Venezia tomorrow. The declaration will accuse the League of Nations of adopting resolutions aimed at putting Italy to death. Consequently, the Italian Prime Minister will attack all countries responsible for this resolution of the League of Nations and state that "Italy will distinguish between the good and the enemies, and will pass on the lessons we have learned to our descendants, and will never forget them." (Havas, 27th)
