US Reply to the League of Nations; Declares Adherence to International Treaties; Upholds Peace Second to None; Strives to Avoid Getting Caught in the Vortex of War

(Washington) The U.S. government has drafted a reply to the memorandum issued by the League of Nations regarding sanctions against Italy, stating, "The U.S. government and people deeply respect current international treaties. If there are mutual suspicions or differences of opinion among the countries of the world, they should be resolved by peaceful means. No country, once it has signed various treaties, has the right to disregard or refuse to comply with them. As for the current Italo-Abyssinian dispute, the U.S. government has done its best to assist within its possible scope in maintaining peace and has reiterated the various principles stated in the Paris Peace Pact and the various obligations borne by the signatory countries to the pact. It has also repeatedly expressed the confidence of the entire U.S. people that if the current dispute cannot be resolved peacefully, the results will inevitably lead to a global conflagration. However, the U.S. government has taken various measures in the hope of restoring peace and will always pay attention with sympathy to the efforts of other countries to maintain peace and shorten the war." (Havas, 26th)

(Washington) Secretary of State Hull notified the League of Nations tonight that although the U.S. government approves of the League of Nations' efforts, it does not wish to participate directly. The U.S. government is sympathetically interested in the individual or collective efforts of other countries to maintain peace and to try to localize the war in Italy. However, the U.S. will still act independently, and the U.S. government's main objective is to avoid getting caught in the vortex of war. Therefore, it does not wish to be involved in any disputes and conflicts arising from the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. The notification avoids mentioning the League of Nations' sanctions action, but it details the U.S.'s actions and policies and solemnly declares that the U.S. took these actions before other countries. (National Telegram, 26th)

(Washington) The government is currently preparing a reply to the memorandum issued by the League of Nations regarding sanctions against Italy. It is generally believed that the content of the reply, in addition to restating the policy decided by the U.S. since the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, will also call for peace. It is rumored that the U.S. government has been conducting secret talks with Britain for a week, promising to support Britain's current policy within the scope permitted by U.S. domestic policy, and attaching an exchange condition, namely that Britain should support the U.S.'s views at the future naval conference and not grant Japan equal ratios. (Havas, 26th)

Supporting Collective Peace; The Key to British Diplomatic Policy; Joint Election Manifesto of the Three Government Leaders; National Defense Plan Limited to Imperial Security

(London) The three-party government (Conservative Party, National Labour Party, National Liberal Party) recently issued a joint election manifesto, co-signed by the three party leaders Baldwin, MacDonald, and Simon. The first paragraph of the manifesto states that Britain has always been loyal to the League of Nations, which is the "key to British foreign policy." In the future, it will strive to make the League of Nations even more effective. "Regarding the current negotiations on the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, we will strive to continue to pursue the hope of achieving a fair resolution within the scope of the League of Nations that can be jointly accepted by the League of Nations and Italy and Abyssinia." The second paragraph strongly supports the principle of collective security, but states that Britain's defense forces must be strengthened to fulfill their obligations. However, the national defense plan that the government will submit to the next parliament will be limited to what is necessary for imperial security. The benefits that arms manufacturers can obtain must be limited to prevent them from being excessive. At the same time, the government will continue to strive for the conclusion of an international disarmament convention. The manifesto then mentions the convening of a naval conference. Britain earnestly hopes that the naval conference will achieve concrete results. Furthermore, the manifesto also mentions economic issues, stating that the government intends to follow the example created by the Ottawa Conference and implement an international trade policy. The government will strive to reduce tariff barriers. Regarding agricultural policy, it will seek to expand the domestic market. In addition, it will establish new public works projects or promote an unemployment insurance system to benefit farmers and workers, and the education and alimony systems will also be reformed. Finally, the manifesto explains the internal divisions of the Labour Party. (Havas, 27th)

French Radical Socialist Party Congress; Passes Six Resolutions; Maintains Friendship Between Britain and Italy; Right-Wing Activities Should Be Banned

(Paris) The Radical Socialist Party Congress continued to meet here today. It unanimously passed a declaration, putting forward the following six proposals: (1) To maintain a loyal attitude towards all of France's friendly nations, especially Britain and Italy; (2) Regarding the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, to implement financial sanctions against the aggressor country in accordance with the provisions of the League of Nations Covenant, but still to continue to strive for a solution that respects the interests of all parties; (3) To disarm all enemies of the Republic; (4) To stabilize the currency and oppose inflation; (5) To assist agriculture; (6) To establish public works projects to reduce the number of unemployed. (Havas, 27th)

(Paris) Today, the Radical Socialist Party held a congress here and passed a compromise resolution on the dispute over the actions to be taken against the Fascist League. The general public was initially afraid that the Radical Socialist Party would order its members in the cabinet to resign, thereby overthrowing the government, but now they have been relieved of this concern. The resolution extends the government's lifespan and requires the next House to convene. Its first action should be to discuss various proposals authorizing the government to dissolve the Fascist League and prohibit quasi-military exercises. Former Prime Minister Daladier delivered a fierce speech at the meeting, vehemently criticizing the Fascist League, saying that they had formulated a plan to encircle Paris and use Hitler's methods in France. (Reuter, 26th)

Fascist Party Anniversary; Italian Army Prepares for a Major Offensive; General Offensive on the Northern Route Aims for Magal; Abyssinian Army Firmly Defends Key Passes to Resist the Powerful Enemy

Addis Ababa According to a telegram from our special correspondent O'Chana, a report has been received here from the front lines stating that an Italian army offensive is imminent. It is predicted that the Italian army will begin its advance tomorrow, the anniversary of the Fascist Party's march on Rome. The Abyssinian military authorities have instructed all units to prepare for resistance. General Walde, commander of the Golahei fortress on the southern route, and General Seyoum, commander-in-chief of the northern route, have also announced separately that the Italian army is currently busy mobilizing and will soon begin its offensive. In addition, General Gasa, commander of the forward troops on the left wing of the Abyssinian army on the northern route, will come into contact with the Italian army in a short period of time. It is generally predicted that the major battle will unfold north of the city of Magal. (Havas, 27th)

(Rome) According to unconfirmed reports from Eritrea, three Italian army corps have now simultaneously launched an offensive towards Magal, which is the main destination for the Italian army's advance on the northern front. In the center, troops from Italian Somaliland, before dawn this morning, advanced from Adajahamud along the main road to Magal. Magal is 65 miles southeast of Adowa and has now reached Debrasion. Other troops advanced from the holy city of Aksum along the narrow passes of Recla and Aimanot, encountering only a few isolated instances of resistance along the way. According to experts, it will be more difficult for the Italian army to capture Magal than to occupy Adowa because the town of Magal is located on a slope facing north. (Reuter, 27th)

(Rome) Military figures claim that the Italian army is currently launching operations on both the northern and southern fronts in Abyssinia, hoping to open up a route from Eritrea to Italian Somaliland. On the northern front, after the Blackshirt Division "Diamante" occupied the area of Adunekfac, the Italian army units stationed in the Tigre province have now formed a united front. The purpose of this Italian offensive is to occupy the city of Magal. However, the area between the city of Adowa and the city of Magal, passing through the Tombien region, is entirely mountainous. All the key passes on the mountains have been fortified and defended by the Abyssinian army. The Italian Air Force has now begun bombing Abyssinian army positions and will soon use heavy artillery to cover the infantry's advance. If advancing from the Italian army's front lines, there are three roads that lead to the city of Magal. However, all three roads must pass through mountainous terrain. The people of the Seyman tribe west of the city are quite sympathetic to the Italian army, which should facilitate the Italian army's advance from that direction. However, the Abyssinian army has now fortified the town of Amba Aradam, which is 3,400 meters above sea level. The Italian army will have to pass through this town to reach the city of Taesy from the northern front lines, and the Abyssinian army will inevitably put up fierce resistance when the Italian army reaches the town. As far as the eastern route is concerned, since the Italian army occupied the Musa Ali mountain area, the port of Assab in the Italian colony of Eritrea is now safe. As for the southern front, people in the Italian colony of Somaliland believe that once the Italian army occupies the various military roads in the Ogaden region, the various tribes in the region will not be difficult to submit to the Italian army. (Havas, 27th)

Another Key City Falls on the Southern Route

(Rome) Elite African Dubat troops in the Italian army launched a surprise attack on Friday on the southern front and captured the key city of Callaho in the Shabeli district. The unit recently occupied Daggahai, then pursued the retreating Abyssinian soldiers. They then encountered a large army led by Bati, and engaged in fierce fighting. Bati was killed in action, and his troops were completely routed. The unit then took advantage of the victory to advance rapidly towards Callaho. The defending troops initially did not expect the enemy troops to approach so quickly and responded in a panic, then abandoned the city and fled. As a result, the key city located on the top of the mountain fell into the hands of the Italian army. (Reuter, 27th)

Aircraft bombed the Abyssinian outposts protecting Dagabur, indicating that General Graziani is feigning an attack on the Shabelle River line and is actually advancing towards Jijiga. Currently, the Abyssinian army in Jijiga is still holding its position, watching to see which route the Italian army will take. (National Telegram, 26th)

Harar According to a report from our correspondent Lavoya, news has come from the southern front that the Italian army is currently advancing rapidly and will soon engage in a major battle with the Abyssinian army. The Abyssinian authorities in Harar province have been at odds with the farmers because the army has always relied on the people for food and arbitrarily requisitioned food and utensils. A special military supply office has now been established to ease the tension between the military and the people. Twelve trucks, fully loaded with food, left here yesterday to supply the regular army. (Havas, 26th)

Golahei Radio Station Loses Contact

Addis Ababa The Abyssinian King received a telegram from General Seyoum, commander-in-chief of the northern route, stating that the Italian army's actions along the Aksum, Adowa, and Adigrat lines in the Tigre region indicate that the Italian army is now preparing for a general offensive or may begin tomorrow. The Abyssinian King has now issued a notice to commanders on all routes to guard against a general Italian offensive and has informed them that the Italian army may use Harar as one of its offensive targets. It is generally believed here that the Italian army has begun attacking Golahei, the center of Ogaden, and has destroyed the radio station there, because the radio station used to send telegrams twice a day, but in the past 24 hours, there has been no news. The authorities here are therefore quite anxious. (Reuter, 27th)

Italian Army on the Northern Route Forms a Link

Tigre Province Front Lines Soldiers on the right wing of the Italian army have recently occupied the area of Adunekfac (on the Feresmainti River). The purpose of this action is to allow the troops of General Maravigna and General Sandini stationed at Aksum and Adigrat to form a united front in the area of Adunekfac. (Havas, 27th)

Tigre Province Front Lines The Italian army is actively building roads in this province. The road from Mareb through Enticho to Tzalca, built jointly by soldiers and party troops, has been completed. Lieutenant General Battoglio, Chief of the Army General Staff, and Leschana, Undersecretary of the Colonies, held a commissioning ceremony. (Havas, 26th)

Home
